25:T28b5,<entryFree id="n3283" key="لَا أَبَالِيهِ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>3</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">لَا أَبَالِيهِ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> is from <foreign lang="ar">البلآء</foreign>, [inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">بَلَاهُ</foreign>,] so that it signifies [properly] <hi rend="ital">I shall not,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I do not, care for him, mind him, heed him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">regard him, so as to share with him my trial and his trial:</hi> (Ham p. 94:) [and hence,] one says thus, (S, Mgh, Msb,) or <foreign lang="ar">مَا أَبَالِيهِ</foreign>, (M, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَالِىبِهِ</foreign>, (Mgh, Msb,) or <foreign lang="ar">مَا أُبَالِى بِهِ</foreign>, (MF, TA,) but the verb is more chastely made trans. without the preposition <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign>, (A, TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">مُبَالَاةٌ</foreign> (M, Mgh, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">بِلَآءٌ</foreign> (M, K, TA [in the CK, erroneously, <foreign lang="ar">بَلاء</foreign>]) and <foreign lang="ar">بَالَةٌ</foreign> (T, S, M, Mgh, Msb, K,) said by some to be a quasi-inf. n. and by others to be an inf. n., (MF, TA,) [in the T it is said to be a subst., from <foreign lang="ar">المُبَالَاةُ</foreign>,] originally <foreign lang="ar">بَالِيَةٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">عَافِيَةٌ</foreign> from <foreign lang="ar">عَافَاهُ</foreign>, (T, S, Mgh, Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">بَالٌ</foreign>, [which is more strange,] (M, K,) meaning [merely] <hi rend="ital">I shall not,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I do not, care for, mind, heed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">regard, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it;</hi> (S, Mgh, Msb, K;) <hi rend="ital">I shall not be,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I am not, disquieted by him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it:</hi> (Mgh, Msb:) or, as some say, <foreign lang="ar">لَا أُبَالِيهِ</foreign> is formed by transposition from <foreign lang="ar">لَا أُبَاوِلُهُ</foreign>, from <foreign lang="ar">البَالُ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">I will not,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I do not, cause him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, to move,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">occur to, my mind; nor give,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pay, any attention to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it:</hi> (Z, TA: [and the like is said in the T:]) or the proper [or literal] meaning is, <hi rend="ital">I will not,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I do not, contend with him for superiority in goodness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">excellence, by reason of my little care,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">regard, for him:</hi> (Mgh:) or it was employed to denote the contending with another for superiority in glory, or excellence, as will be shown by the citation of a verse in the latter portion of this paragraph; and then, in consequence of frequency of usage, came to denote contempt, or mean estimation: (Ham p. 31:) or its original meaning is, <hi rend="ital">I will not,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I do not, strive with him to be first; neglecting him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">leaving him to himself;</hi> from <foreign lang="ar">تَبَالَى القَوْمُ</foreign> as explained below; see 6. (Msb.) It is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">لَا يُبَالِيهِمُ ٱللّٰهُ بَالَةً</foreign>, or, accord. to one reading, <foreign lang="ar">لَا يُبَالِى بِهِمْ بَالَةً</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">God will not hold them to be of any value or weight.</hi> (TA.) And in another, <foreign lang="ar">هٰؤُلآءِ فِى الجَنَّةِ وَلَا أُبَالِى وَهٰؤُلَآءِ فِى النَّارِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَلَا أُبَالِى</foreign>, said to mean [<hi rend="ital">These</hi> will be <hi rend="ital">in Paradise, and] I shall not disapprove;</hi> [<hi rend="ital">and these</hi> will be <hi rend="ital">in the fire</hi> of Hell,] <hi rend="ital">and I shall not disapprove.</hi> (Az, TA.) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">لَا أُبَالِى مَا صَنَعْتَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I shall not,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I do not, care for what thou didst,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hast done</hi>]. (IDrd, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">مَا أُبَالِى أَقُمْتَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَمْ قَعَدْتَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I care not whether thou stand or sit</hi>]: and <foreign lang="ar">مَا أُبَالِى بِقِيَامِكَ وَعَدَمِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I care not for thy standing and thy not doing so</hi>]. (Mughnee in art. <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">مَا بَالَيْتُ بِهِ</foreign> (AZ, Msb, TA) <hi rend="ital">I did not care for, mind,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">regard, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">بَالَى بِالشَّىْءِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He cared for the thing;</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">he was disquieted by the thing.</hi> (T.) The verb is sometimes thus used, in an affirmative manner; (Ham p. 94; [and the like is said in the TA;]) though some say that it is not; (Msb;) but it is not unless it occurs with a negative in the former part of the sentence or in the latter part thereof; as when one says, <foreign lang="ar">مَا بَالَى بِكَ صَدِيقُكَ وَلٰكِنْ بَالَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَبْدُكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Thy friend cared not for thee, but thy slave cared</hi>]; and as in the saying of Zuheyr, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">لَقَدْ بَالَيْتُ مَظْعَنَ أُمِّ أَوْفَى</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَلٰكِنْ أُمُّ أَوْفَى لَا تُبَالِى</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Verily I cared for the departure of Umm-Owfà, but Umm-Owfà cares not</hi>]. (Ham p. 94.) One says also, <foreign lang="ar">لَمْ أُبَالِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لَمْ أُبَلْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I did not care,</hi> &amp;c.]: (T, S, M, Mgh, Msb, K: [but in the CK the latter of these is omitted:]) in the latter the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> [of prolongation] is suppressed for the purpose of alleviating the utterance, like as <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> is suppressed in the inf. n. [or quasi-inf. n.] <foreign lang="ar">بَالَةٌ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, Msb,) originally <foreign lang="ar">بَالِيَةٌ</foreign>, (S, Msb,) and in <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَدْرِ</foreign>: (S:) or the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> is suppressed in this case to avoid the concurrence of two quiescent letters; (Kh, Sb, M, IB;) not for the purpose of alleviating the utterance; (IB, TA;) for this is done because the <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign> is made quiescent. (Kh, Sb, M.) And, accord. to Kh, (Sb, M,) some of the Arabs say, <foreign lang="ar">لَمْ أُبَلِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I did not care for him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it</hi>], (Sb, M,) or <foreign lang="ar">لَمْ أُبَلِ</foreign>, [in the CK, erroneously, <foreign lang="ar">لم اَبْلِ</foreign>,] with kesr to the <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign>; (K, TA;) [for <foreign lang="ar">لم أُبَالِهِ</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar">لم أُبَالِ</foreign>;] only suppressing the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign>, as they do in <foreign lang="ar">عُلَبِطٌ</foreign> [for <foreign lang="ar">عُلَابِطٌ</foreign>]. (Sb, S, M.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  IAar says that <foreign lang="ar">بَالَى</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">مُبَالَاةٌ</foreign>, is like   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n3283-1" target="أَبْلَى" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">He exerted himself in a description of a war,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">battle, or of generous conduct;</hi> as when one says, <foreign lang="ar">أَبْلَى ذٰلِكَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">اليَوْمَ بَلَآءً حَسَنًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He exerted himself well, that day, in a description of war,</hi> &amp;c.]: and he cites the following verse [to which reference has been made above]: <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَأَنْتَ قَدْمَتَّ مِنَ الهُزَالِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">What hath happened to me that I see thee standing exerting thyself in a description of generous qualities, when thou hast become</hi> like one <hi rend="ital">dead by reason of leanness?</hi>]: he says that he [the poet] heard him [whom he thus addresses] saying, “ We have eaten and we have drunk [with guests], and we have done [such and such things]; ” enumerating, or recounting, generous qualities or actions, and lying in doing so: (T, TA:) in another place he says that <foreign lang="ar">تُبَالِى</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">looking to see which of them</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">of thee and others</hi>] <hi rend="ital">is best in</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بال</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">state,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">condition</hi>], <hi rend="ital">while thou art dying:</hi> (TA:) he says, also, that <foreign lang="ar">بَالَاهُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">مُبَالَاةٌ</foreign>, signifies <hi rend="ital">he contended with him for superiority in glory,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">excellence;</hi> (T, TA; *) and [it is said that] <foreign lang="ar">تبالى</foreign>

                  <foreign lang="ar">بِكَذَا</foreign> (vulg. <foreign lang="ar">اِبْتَلَى</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">He was tried, proved,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tested, by,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">with, such a thing;</hi> generally meaning <hi rend="ital">he was afflicted thereby,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">therewith;</hi> as, for instance, by, or with, a disease.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">He asked,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sought,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">desired, of him information,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">news,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tidings.</hi> (M, K.) And <foreign lang="ar">ابتلى</foreign> signifies also <hi rend="ital">He conjured,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">adjured, and asked if any had knowledge;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">اِسْتَحْلَفَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">اِسْتَعْرَفَ</foreign> [explained by what here follows]. [In the CK, both the verb and the explanation are here wrong: the former is written <foreign lang="ar">اُبْلِىَ</foreign>; and the latter, <foreign lang="ar">اسْتُحْلِفَ و اسْتُعْرِفَ</foreign>.]) A poet says, <quote>
                     <L>

                     </L>

                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">She seeks for her father among the travellingcompanions, and conjures,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">adjures, and asks. if any have knowledge, when a crocodile has destroyed him in the depth of the great river:</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تَبَغَّى</foreign> is for <foreign lang="ar">تَتَبَغَّى</foreign>]: he means that she says to them, “ I conjure you, or adjure you, by God, (<foreign lang="ar">نَاشَدْتُكُمْ ٱللّٰهَ</foreign>,) [tell me,] do ye know any tidings of my father? ” (M, TA.)
